{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01XK3yjgikxEYmUC4gnKFwiG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01CNMiDgncYHcC1mntkBDhdH","name":"Write","input":{"path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nAnalysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` against the test suite in\n`test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test{,_2,_3}.cc` reveals several untested or\nunder-tested code paths. The most critical gaps involve the premature-reset drain\nlogic (which could cause connection leaks or runaway recursion), the immediate\n(non-graceful) GOAWAY path, and the HTTP/1.0 keep-alive response logic. These\ngaps expose potential denial-of-service vectors, correctness regressions, and\nincorrect HTTP/1.0 framing behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` — Early-threshold Drain and Recursion Guard\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~702–748\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` contains two distinct logic branches:\n  1. **Early-exit threshold** (line 731): when `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit`\n     even though `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, the connection\n     is drained preemptively. This branch is never exercised in existing tests.\n  2. **Recursion guard** (lines 716–718): the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag\n     prevents infinite recursion when `resetAllStreams()` triggers further stream\n     destructions. No test forces a scenario where this flag is actually set and\n     the guard fires.\n  The `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat is never asserted in any\n  `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` file.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DrainsDueToTooManyPrematureResets)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a low limit via runtime override\n  (`overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 4`,\n  `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 100`).\n  Create 4 HTTP/2 streams; reset each before sending a response within the\n  minimum lifetime window so each counts as a premature reset.\n  Assertions:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value() == 1`\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(_, _))` is triggered.\n\n  A second test `DrainsDueToEarlyThresholdPrematureResets` should set `limit = 10`\n  but trigger 6 premature resets out of 6 total streams (i.e., all are premature),\n  hitting the early-threshold branch before the total reaches 10.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  If the early-threshold path is broken, an attacker sending many short-lived\n  streams that are never answered can exhaust server resources without hitting the\n  total-stream count threshold. If the recursion guard is broken, a malicious\n  client could trigger a stack overflow by timing many resets to all complete\n  during the same drain sequence.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` — Immediate Non-Graceful GOAWAY\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797–823\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose` has two branches:\n  - `graceful == true` → calls `startDrainSequence()`, sets `go_away_sent_ = true`.\n    Tested in `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`.\n  - `graceful == false` → calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, then `codec_->goAway()`\n    **immediately**, sets `go_away_sent_ = true`, and calls `doConnectionClose(...,\n    \"forced_goaway\")` (lines 818–822).\n  The non-graceful branch is entirely absent from the test suite. Additionally,\n  the idempotency guard (`go_away_sent_` flag, lines 800–802) is only exercised\n  for the graceful path; repeated calls with `graceful == false` are untested.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate)\n  ```\n  Setup: HTTP/2 connection with one active stream. A decoder filter calls\n  `filter->callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, shutdownNotice())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, goAway())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(..., \"forced_goaway\"))`.\n\n  A second test `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediateIdempotent` calls\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` twice and verifies codec methods are called\n  only once thanks to the `go_away_sent_` guard.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A filter that needs to immediately terminate a connection (e.g., due to a\n  detected security violation) will silently fail to send the codec-level GOAWAY\n  if this path is broken. The client would receive no indication that the\n  connection was aborted by the proxy.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: `validateHeaders` — `InvalidTransferEncoding` Returns 501 Not Implemented\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1197–1254 (with focus on lines 1218–1220)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  Inside `validateHeaders()`, when the UHV validation fails with\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding` as the failure detail,\n  the response code is set to `Code::NotImplemented` (HTTP 501) rather than the\n  usual `Code::BadRequest` (HTTP 400):\n  ```cpp\n  Code response_code =\n      failure_details == Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding\n          ? Code::NotImplemented\n          : Code::BadRequest;\n  ```\n  No test in the suite provides a header validator that returns this specific\n  failure detail and then verifies a 501 response is sent. All header-validation\n  tests assert 400 responses.\n  Also untested: the `streamErrorOnlyErrors()` helper (lines 1119–1126) which\n  guards whether `handleCodecError()` is called for certain UHV error details\n  (`FragmentInUrlPath`, `EscapedSlashesInPath`, `Percent00InPath`). Those paths\n  avoid closing the connection even when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is\n  false.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTransferEncodingReturns501)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a custom `ServerHeaderValidator` (via the `header_validator_`\n  mock) that returns a failure with detail equal to\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding`. Send an HTTP/1.1\n  request through `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(response_encoder_, encodeHeaders(HeaderHasStatus(501), _))`.\n  - `downstream_rq_4xx_` is NOT incremented (501 is a 5xx).\n  - `downstream_rq_5xx_` IS incremented.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP intermediaries must return 501 for unrecognized transfer-encoding per\n  RFC 7230 §3.3.1. If the branch silently sends 400 instead, the client receives\n  ambiguous error information and may retry an unretryable error, causing\n  request amplification.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: HTTP/1.0 Keep-Alive Response Header in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938–1948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  In `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, when the downstream codec is HTTP/1.0 AND\n  the response includes a `Content-Length` header (so connection framing is\n  defined without close), Envoy must set `Connection: keep-alive` to allow\n  connection reuse:\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n  Existing HTTP/1.0 tests (in `conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc`, e.g.,\n  `ConnectionDurationSafeHttp1`) focus on connection duration and soft-drain\n  behavior. None of them exercise the path where a 200 response with\n  `Content-Length` is sent over an HTTP/1.0 connection and verify that\n  `Connection: keep-alive` is present in the response.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, Http10ResponseWithContentLengthSetsKeepAlive)\n  ```\n  Setup: `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, protocol()).WillRepeatedly(Return(Protocol::Http10))`.\n  Dispatch an HTTP/1.0 GET request. Encode a response with `{\":status\", \"200\"}` and\n  `{\"content-length\", \"5\"}`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The response headers passed to `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders` contain\n    `Connection: keep-alive`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is false.\n\n  A companion test `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthSetsClose` verifies\n  that omitting `Content-Length` causes `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n  to be true and `Connection: close` is added.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  If `Connection: keep-alive` is missing on HTTP/1.0 responses that do include\n  a body length, downstream HTTP/1.0 clients will close the connection after\n  every response, eliminating connection reuse and creating connection-pool\n  churn. Conversely, if the Content-Length-absent path is broken, the proxy\n  could fail to close the connection at the right time, leaving HTTP/1.0 clients\n  hanging indefinitely.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Route-Level Idle Timeout of Zero Disables Stream Idle Timer in `refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2346–2378\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  `refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts()` handles the case where a route-level\n  `idleTimeout()` is configured as zero milliseconds, which is an explicit\n  override to disable any stream idle timeout. In that case, an active\n  `stream_idle_timer_` (created at the HCM/global level) must be disabled and\n  nulled out (lines 2364–2368):\n  ```cpp\n  } else if (stream_idle_timer_ != nullptr) {\n    // If we had a global stream idle timeout but the route-level idle timeout is\n    // set to zero (to override), we disable the idle timer.\n    stream_idle_timer_->disableTimer();\n    stream_idle_timer_ = nullptr;\n  }\n  ```\n  All existing `PerStreamIdleTimeout*` tests set non-zero route idle timeouts.\n  No test configures a global HCM stream idle timeout, then routes to a route\n  entry with `idleTimeout()` returning `std::chrono::milliseconds(0)`, and\n  verifies that the timer is disabled.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, RouteIdleTimeoutZeroDisablesGlobalIdleTimer)\n  ```\n  Setup:\n  - Set `stream_idle_timeout_ = std::chrono::milliseconds(30)` on the HCM config\n    (so a global stream idle timer is created in `ActiveStream` constructor).\n  - `ON_CALL(route_config_provider_.route_config_->route_->route_entry_,\n       idleTimeout()).WillByDefault(Return(std::chrono::milliseconds(0)))`.\n  - Dispatch a request and process headers so `setVirtualHostRoute` is called.\n  Assertions:\n  - The idle timer mock should have `disableTimer()` called and after that the\n    timer should not fire even if the simulated clock advances by 30ms.\n  - No 408 response is sent for a request that is still in flight after 30ms.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A route operator who sets an explicit zero idle timeout to exempt long-polling\n  endpoints (e.g., SSE streams or webhook listeners) from the global stream idle\n  timeout will instead see those streams time out unexpectedly if this path\n  is broken. This can cause silent connection drops on intentionally long-lived\n  streams.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: QUIC Deferred Access Logging in `doDeferredStreamDestroy`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~362–375\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When `codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3` and the runtime feature flag\n  `envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener` is enabled,\n  `doDeferredStreamDestroy` calls `stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers()` instead\n  of immediately calling `stream.log(AccessLog::AccessLogType::DownstreamEnd)`.\n  ```cpp\n  if (codec_ && codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3 &&\n      !stream.filter_manager_.sawDownstreamReset() &&\n      stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n      Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\n          \"envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener\")) {\n    stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers();\n  } else {\n    stream.log(AccessLog::AccessLogType::DownstreamEnd);\n  }\n  ```\n  No test in `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` exercises this HTTP/3 deferred logging\n  path. The most critical gaps involve the premature-reset drain\nlogic (which could cause connection leaks or runaway recursion), the immediate\n(non-graceful) GOAWAY path, and the HTTP/1.0 keep-alive response logic. These\ngaps expose potential denial-of-service vectors, correctness regressions, and\nincorrect HTTP/1.0 framing behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` — Early-Threshold Drain and Recursion Guard\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~702–748\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` contains two distinct logic branches that\n  are both absent from the test suite:\n  1. **Early-exit threshold** (line 731): when\n     `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit` even though\n     `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, the connection is\n     drained preemptively. If the recursion guard is broken, a\n  carefully timed sequence of resets could cause a stack overflow inside\n  `resetAllStreams`.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` — Immediate Non-Graceful GOAWAY\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797–823\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose` has two branches:\n  - `graceful == true` (lines 808–815): calls `startDrainSequence()` and sets\n    `go_away_sent_ = true`. Covered by `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`.\n  - `graceful == false` (lines 817–823): calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, then\n    `codec_->goAway()` **immediately**, sets `go_away_sent_ = true`, and calls\n    `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`.\n  The non-graceful branch is entirely absent from the test suite. Additionally,\n  the idempotency guard (`go_away_sent_` check at lines 800–802) is exercised\n  only through the graceful path; repeated calls with `graceful == false` are\n  untested.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate)\n  ```\n  Setup: HTTP/2 connection with one active stream. A decoder filter calls\n  `filter->callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, shutdownNotice())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, goAway())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay, _))` fires with detail `\"forced_goaway\"`.\n\n  A second test `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediateIdempotent` calls\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` twice from the filter and verifies that\n  `codec_->shutdownNotice()` and `codec_->goAway()` are each called only once.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A filter that must immediately terminate a connection (e.g., upon detecting a\n  security policy violation) will silently fail to send the codec-level GOAWAY\n  frame if this path is broken. The client receives no signal that the\n  connection was intentionally terminated by the proxy, making debugging and\n  compliance auditing very difficult.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: `validateHeaders` — `InvalidTransferEncoding` Returns 501 Not Implemented\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1197–1254 (focus on lines 1218–1220 and 1119–1126)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  Inside `validateHeaders()`, when the header validator fails with\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding` as the failure detail,\n  the response code is `Code::NotImplemented` (HTTP 501) rather than\n  `Code::BadRequest` (HTTP 400):\n  ```cpp\n  Code response_code =\n      failure_details == Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding\n          ? Code::NotImplemented\n          : Code::BadRequest;\n  ```\n  No existing test provides a header validator that returns this specific failure\n  detail and then verifies a 501 response. All header-validation tests assert 400.\n\n  Also untested: the `streamErrorOnlyErrors()` helper (lines 1119–1126), which\n  controls whether `handleCodecError()` is called for specific UHV error details\n  (`FragmentInUrlPath`, `EscapedSlashesInPath`, `Percent00InPath`). These paths\n  skip connection closure even when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false,\n  and no test verifies the distinction.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTransferEncodingReturns501)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a mock `ServerHeaderValidator` (assign to `header_validator_`\n  in the test) that fails validation with detail\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding`. The most critical gaps involve the premature-reset drain\nlogic (which could cause connection leaks or runaway recursion), the immediate\n(non-graceful) GOAWAY path, and the HTTP/1.0 keep-alive response logic. These\ngaps expose potential denial-of-service vectors, correctness regressions, and\nincorrect HTTP/1.0 framing behavior.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` — Early-Threshold Drain and Recursion Guard\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~702–748\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` contains two distinct logic branches that\n  are both absent from the test suite:\n  1. **Early-exit threshold** (line 731): when\n     `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= limit` even though\n     `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit`, the connection is\n     drained preemptively. This early-close branch has never been exercised.\n  2. **Recursion guard** (lines 716–718): the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`\n     flag prevents infinite recursion when `resetAllStreams()` itself triggers\n     further stream destructions that re-enter `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`.\n     No test verifies that this guard actually fires and breaks the recursion.\n  The stat `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is never asserted in any\n  `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` file.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, DrainsDueToTooManyPrematureResets)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a low total-stream limit via runtime override\n  (`overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count = 4`,\n  `overload.premature_reset_min_stream_lifetime_seconds = 100` so every\n  short-lived reset qualifies). Create 4 HTTP/2 streams; reset each one\n  before sending any response (no `responseCode()` set), so each counts as a\n  premature reset.\n  Assertions:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value() == 1`\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(_, _))` fires.\n\n  A companion test `DrainsDueToEarlyThresholdPrematureResets` sets `limit = 10`\n  but triggers 6 premature resets out of 6 total streams — all premature —\n  hitting the early-threshold branch before the total reaches 10.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  If the early-threshold path is broken, an attacker sending many short-lived\n  streams that are never answered can exhaust server resources without hitting\n  the total-stream count threshold. If the recursion guard is broken, a\n  carefully timed sequence of resets could cause a stack overflow inside\n  `resetAllStreams`.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` — Immediate Non-Graceful GOAWAY\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797–823\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose` has two branches:\n  - `graceful == true` (lines 808–815): calls `startDrainSequence()` and sets\n    `go_away_sent_ = true`. Covered by `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`.\n  - `graceful == false` (lines 817–823): calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, then\n    `codec_->goAway()` **immediately**, sets `go_away_sent_ = true`, and calls\n    `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`.\n  The non-graceful branch is entirely absent from the test suite. Additionally,\n  the idempotency guard (`go_away_sent_` check at lines 800–802) is exercised\n  only through the graceful path; repeated calls with `graceful == false` are\n  untested.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate)\n  ```\n  Setup: HTTP/2 connection with one active stream. A decoder filter calls\n  `filter->callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, shutdownNotice())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, goAway())` fires exactly once.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(filter_callbacks_.connection_, close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay, _))` fires with detail `\"forced_goaway\"`.\n\n  A second test `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediateIdempotent` calls\n  `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` twice from the filter and verifies that\n  `codec_->shutdownNotice()` and `codec_->goAway()` are each called only once.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A filter that must immediately terminate a connection (e.g., upon detecting a\n  security policy violation) will silently fail to send the codec-level GOAWAY\n  frame if this path is broken. The client receives no signal that the\n  connection was intentionally terminated by the proxy, making debugging and\n  compliance auditing very difficult.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: `validateHeaders` — `InvalidTransferEncoding` Returns 501 Not Implemented\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1197–1254 (focus on lines 1218–1220 and 1119–1126)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  Inside `validateHeaders()`, when the header validator fails with\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding` as the failure detail,\n  the response code is `Code::NotImplemented` (HTTP 501) rather than\n  `Code::BadRequest` (HTTP 400):\n  ```cpp\n  Code response_code =\n      failure_details == Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding\n          ? Code::NotImplemented\n          : Code::BadRequest;\n  ```\n  No existing test provides a header validator that returns this specific failure\n  detail and then verifies a 501 response. All header-validation tests assert 400.\n\n  Also untested: the `streamErrorOnlyErrors()` helper (lines 1119–1126), which\n  controls whether `handleCodecError()` is called for specific UHV error details\n  (`FragmentInUrlPath`, `EscapedSlashesInPath`, `Percent00InPath`). These paths\n  skip connection closure even when `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` is false,\n  and no test verifies the distinction.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, InvalidTransferEncodingReturns501)\n  ```\n  Setup: configure a mock `ServerHeaderValidator` (assign to `header_validator_`\n  in the test) that fails validation with detail\n  `Http1ResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidTransferEncoding`. Send an HTTP/1.1\n  request through `decodeHeaders`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The response encoder receives headers with `:status: 501`.\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_5xx_.value() == 1` (not 4xx).\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_protocol_error_.value() == 0` (stream-only\n    error; connection not closed).\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.1 requires a 501 response for unknown or invalid transfer-encoding\n  (RFC 7230 §3.3.1). If the branch silently returns 400, clients receive an\n  ambiguous error and may retry a request that is fundamentally unretryable,\n  causing request amplification. The `streamErrorOnlyErrors` gap additionally\n  risks premature connection teardown for requests carrying URL fragments,\n  breaking browser prefetch and analytics pipelines that legitimately include\n  fragment identifiers.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: HTTP/1.0 Keep-Alive Response Header in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938–1948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  In `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, when the codec is HTTP/1.0 AND the response\n  includes a `Content-Length` header (so body framing is defined without\n  connection close), Envoy must set `Connection: keep-alive`:\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n  Existing HTTP/1.0 tests (e.g., `ConnectionDurationSafeHttp1` in\n  `conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc`) focus on drain behavior. None of them encode\n  a 200 response with `Content-Length` over an HTTP/1.0 connection and then\n  verify that `Connection: keep-alive` is present in the response.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, Http10ResponseWithContentLengthSetsKeepAlive)\n  ```\n  Setup: `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, protocol()).WillRepeatedly(Return(Protocol::Http10))`.\n  Dispatch an HTTP/1.0 GET request. Encode a response with `{\":status\", \"200\"}`\n  and `{\"content-length\", \"5\"}`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The `ResponseHeaderMap` passed to `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders` contains\n    `Connection: keep-alive`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is `false`.\n\n  A companion test `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthSetsClose` omits\n  `Content-Length` and asserts `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is `true`\n  and the response does NOT contain `Connection: keep-alive`.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  If `Connection: keep-alive` is missing on HTTP/1.0 responses that do include\n  a defined body length, HTTP/1.0 clients will close and reopen the connection\n  after every response, eliminating connection reuse and creating significant\n  connection-pool churn. Conversely, if the no-Content-Length path is broken,\n  Envoy could fail to close the connection promptly, leaving HTTP/1.0 clients\n  hanging indefinitely waiting for a response boundary.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Route-Level Idle Timeout of Zero Disables Stream Idle Timer\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2346–2378\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  `refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts()` handles the case where a route entry's\n  `idleTimeout()` returns `std::chrono::milliseconds(0)`, which is an explicit\n  override meaning \"no idle timeout\". In that case an existing\n  `stream_idle_timer_` (created from the global HCM config) must be disabled\n  and nulled (lines 2364–2368):\n  ```cpp\n  } else if (stream_idle_timer_ != nullptr) {\n    stream_idle_timer_->disableTimer();\n    stream_idle_timer_ = nullptr;\n  }\n  ```\n  All existing `PerStreamIdleTimeout*` tests use non-zero route timeouts. No test\n  sets a global HCM stream idle timeout, then routes to a route entry with\n  `idleTimeout()` returning zero, and verifies the timer is disabled.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, RouteIdleTimeoutZeroDisablesGlobalIdleTimer)\n  ```\n  Setup:\n  - Set `stream_idle_timeout_ = std::chrono::milliseconds(30)` on the HCM config\n    so a global stream idle timer is created in the `ActiveStream` constructor.\n  - `ON_CALL(route_config_provider_.route_config_->route_->route_entry_,\n       idleTimeout()).WillByDefault(Return(std::chrono::milliseconds(0)))`.\n  - Dispatch a request and ensure headers are processed so `setVirtualHostRoute`\n    runs and `refreshIdleAndFlushTimeouts` is called.\n  Assertions:\n  - The idle timer mock should receive `disableTimer()`.\n  - Advancing the simulated clock by 30ms does NOT trigger `onIdleTimeout()`.\n  - No 408 response is sent for a request still in-flight after the global\n    timeout window.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Route operators who set an explicit zero idle timeout to exempt long-polling\n  or streaming endpoints (SSE, webhooks) from the global stream idle timeout\n  will see those streams silently time out if this branch is broken. This\n  causes unexpected connection drops on intentionally long-lived streams\n  without any configuration error being reported.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: HTTP/3 Deferred Access Logging in `doDeferredStreamDestroy`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~362–375\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When `codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3` and the runtime feature flag\n  `envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener` is enabled,\n  `doDeferredStreamDestroy` calls `stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers()` instead\n  of immediately invoking `stream.log(AccessLog::AccessLogType::DownstreamEnd)`:\n  ```cpp\n  if (codec_ && codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http3 &&\n      !stream.filter_manager_.sawDownstreamReset() &&\n      stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n      Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\n          \"envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener\")) {\n    stream.deferHeadersAndTrailers();\n  } else {\n    stream.log(AccessLog::AccessLogType::DownstreamEnd);\n  }\n  ```\n  No test in `conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` exercises this HTTP/3 deferred logging\n  branch. In particular: (a) the happy-path deferral when there is no downstream\n  reset, and (b) the immediate-log fallback when `sawDownstreamReset()` is true\n  even for HTTP/3, are both untested at the HCM layer.\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```\n  TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, Http3DeferredAccessLoggingOnStreamDestroy)\n  ```\n  Setup:\n  - `TestScopedRuntime scoped_runtime; scoped_runtime.mergeValues({{\"envoy.reloadable_features.quic_defer_logging_to_ack_listener\", \"true\"}})`.\n  - `EXPECT_CALL(*codec_, protocol()).WillRepeatedly(Return(Protocol::Http3))`.\n  - Add a `std::shared_ptr<AccessLog::MockInstance>` to `access_logs_`.\n  - Complete a request/response cycle so the stream enters `doDeferredStreamDestroy`.\n  Assertions:\n  - The access log handler's `log()` is NOT called during `doDeferredStreamDestroy`\n    (deferred path taken).\n  - After simulating the QUIC ACK notification that triggers deferred logging,\n    `log()` IS called exactly once.\n\n  A companion test `Http3ImmediateAccessLoggingOnDownstreamReset` triggers a\n  downstream reset before stream completion and asserts that `log()` is called\n  immediately (not deferred), even with the feature flag enabled.\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Deferred QUIC access logging is required for accuracy: logs must capture\n  byte counts and timing only after the ACK, not at the moment the response is\n  handed to the codec. If this path is broken, access logs for HTTP/3 streams\n  record incorrect transmission metrics, undermining billing, SLA monitoring,\n  and capacity-planning data for QUIC deployments.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` | Primary implementation (all gaps located here) |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` | Main test file; gaps 3, 4, 5 most relevant |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` | HTTP/1.0, zombie stream, GOAWAY tests; gaps 1, 2 most relevant |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` | Overload, QUIC, deferred processing tests; gap 6 most relevant |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.h` | Test fixture base (`SetupOpts`, config mock) |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.cc` | Test fixture implementation |\n| `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` | Filter chain execution (referenced by gaps 1, 3) |\n| `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` | Header manipulation (referenced by gap 4) |\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
